<div id="review_2067004725" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2067004725" />
    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29698492-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1397234539p2/29698492.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2067004725?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/29698492-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781681192185" href="/book/show/30038938-tuesdays-at-the-castle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29698492-susan?shelf=no-no-no">no-no-no</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29698492-susan?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2067004725" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6735813955091201489">I started reading this book with such hopes. Unfortunately, these hopes went unfulfilled on two levels, readability and philosophically.<br/><br/>From a readability stand point, this book did nothing for me. I found it dragged and dragged until the last few pages, then all of the action happened all at once, then ended awkwardly. I thought that the characters were also flat and stereotyped so strongly that they were practically caricatures rather than characters. Finally, I also thought that the author wa</span>
  <span id="freeText6735813955091201489" style="display:none">I started reading this book with such hopes. Unfortunately, these hopes went unfulfilled on two levels, readability and philosophically.<br /><br />From a readability stand point, this book did nothing for me. I found it dragged and dragged until the last few pages, then all of the action happened all at once, then ended awkwardly. I thought that the characters were also flat and stereotyped so strongly that they were practically caricatures rather than characters. Finally, I also thought that the author was trying much too hard to be 'cute' and 'funny' and 'clever' and the writing suffered for it - OK, and also really bum and manure jokes?!? - I get that the book is written for children by why insult young people's intelligence in this way? OK, finally, finally it really creeped me out that a 22 year old man was flirting with an 11 year old girl. UGH!<br /><br />From a philosophical stand point, I was clenching my teeth through the entire story, and now I think I must do an energy cleanse for having made it to the end of the book. I added the book to my TBR list because it came up on my feed and I thought 'a clever girl protagonist for a hero - the world needs more of that'. Now all I can see is that the world needs NONE of this! This book is worse than neutral; it is an anti-girl-power novel pretending to be a girl-power book. From page one, literally, the reader learns that 'little girl you can play at being a hero but: understand that it is still men who will control the government (kings, kings, kings - 79 and counting), religion (with male bishop), and academia (with male wizards); if you try and speak out or up too much we will silence you by mocking you and scolding you for having an opinion - unless we are desperate then we might listen; at the end of the day it is still the males who will come to the rescue and solve all the problems, but really do not worry your pretty little head about it - you can still be in charge of food and housekeeping. Oh, and yes, you can also spend your pretty little head worrying about boys, and how you look, and crying and sighing about things.' No, the world needs NO more of this. And, if those so-called traditional gender values are not enough, may I mention that the bad guy has a name starting with kh? Really, the world needs NO more of this. <br /><br />I wish I could give zero (or fewer) stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6735813955091201489" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2082694850?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Collin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Collin" href="/user/show/4971265-collin">Collin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971265-collin?shelf=2017-challenges">2017-challenges</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2082694850" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8801945909030925906">I was genuinely surprised at how much I liked this one. I did it for the PopSugar reading challenge (book with a day/month in the title, obviously) and I wasn't hugely looking forward to it, but it was really, really fun.<br/><br/>The adventures that the royal kids get up to are engaging and while the book ultimately stuck to its MG basis, I was also surprised at how serious things got. This book could easily have been some kind of psychological horror if Jessica Day George had let it go YA or New Adult o</span>
  <span id="freeText8801945909030925906" style="display:none">I was genuinely surprised at how much I liked this one. I did it for the PopSugar reading challenge (book with a day/month in the title, obviously) and I wasn't hugely looking forward to it, but it was really, really fun.<br /><br />The adventures that the royal kids get up to are engaging and while the book ultimately stuck to its MG basis, I was also surprised at how serious things got. This book could easily have been some kind of psychological horror if Jessica Day George had let it go YA or New Adult or something, what with having your actual home murdered (kind of) and being trapped inside. (Like a reverse haunted house? Where the house is the thing being haunted? It was a creepy situation, I don't know.) <br /><br />The ending wobbled - it was too short, and everything settled itself too nicely, too easily. I was really hoping the mystery would go on through the next book, at least, if not through both of the next ones. It was disappointing, so why do I still feel like this books deserves four stars? I'm not usually so generous. But... come on. The siblings are so cute. I really couldn't guess where the plot was going, which is rare in MG. Prince Lulath was wonderful. Princess Celie is the first 11-yo protagonist that I've really loved for a long time. <br /><br />It's just a fun book, last 5 pages notwithstanding. It's just a fun book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8801945909030925906" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rBbwzBHJlLZq4ZcqXbvTPbK8AD2Pb5CIyKSSrwMZ+rSttksMMbgkHAhl8Ulo8/sbdHN5IplgCU6usBtcY0O/Gw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ekXFqSv1C9w9yEmfneNOXq6kaakQEYUslrpP0TMbcR175X5pC4S7dl9ML/yoq2Z4aGsQtgYeHOrwrsYiU0E0sg==')})
  }

She must find Gwen\'s true love to kiss her awake.\n\n\n\nBut who is her true love? The irritating Digby? The happy-go-lucky Prince Andreas, who is holding a contest to find his bride? Joined by one of her father\'s guards, Liam, who happened to be out of the castle when the sleeping spell struck, Annie travels through a fairy tale land populated with characters both familiar and <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3326847451673564445">Jessica Day George likes chocolate, knitting, books, travel, movies, dragons, horses, dogs, and her family. These are all things to keep in mind if you ever meet her. For instance, you could bring her chocolate to make the meeting go more smoothly. You could also talk about how adorable her children are, even if you have never seen them. You could discuss dog breeds (she had a Maltese named Pippin</span>
  <span id="freeText3326847451673564445" style="display:none">Jessica Day George likes chocolate, knitting, books, travel, movies, dragons, horses, dogs, and her family. These are all things to keep in mind if you ever meet her. For instance, you could bring her chocolate to make the meeting go more smoothly. You could also talk about how adorable her children are, even if you have never seen them. You could discuss dog breeds (she had a Maltese named Pippin, and grew up with a poodle mix and a Brittany Spaniel. Right now she has a Coton de Tulear named Sunny). You could talk about Norway, and how it's the Greatest Place On Earth, and Germany, The Second Greatest Place On Earth. You could ask her about yarn, and indicate a willingness to learn to knit your own socks, if you can't already do so.<br /><br />And, well, you could talk about books. Jessica's books, other people's books. It's really all about the books. To paraphrase Jerry Seinfeld: Friends, family, school, they were just obstacles in the way of getting more books.<br /><br />She would like it if books came with chocolate to eat while reading them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3326847451673564445" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
